# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/camel--1006f047` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/camel--1006f047$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Flink DataStream API Deprecation Markers

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/flink under flink-streaming-java/src/ that contain @Deprecated annotations on DataStream API classes or methods. For each deprecated class, identify the class name and the recommended replacement (noted in the deprecation javadoc). Focus on deprecated source functions, sink functions, timestamp extractors, and I/O format classes.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

I found **7 deprecated DataStream API classes and interfaces** in the Apache Flink repository (`github.com/sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc`) under `flink-streaming-java/src/main/java/`:

### Deprecated Classes by Category:

**I/O Format Classes:**

- `TextOutputFormat` - Use Sink-V2 FlinkSink instead

**Source Functions:**
- `DataGeneratorSource` - Use `org.apache.flink.connector.datagen.source.DataGeneratorSource` instead

**Sink Functions:**
- `DiscardingSink` - Use `org.apache.flink.streaming.api.functions.sink.v2.DiscardingSink` instead
- `TwoPhaseCommitSinkFunction` - Use `org.apache.flink.api.connector.sink2.Sink` instead
- `StreamingFileSink` - Use `org.apache.flink.connector.file.sink.FileSink` instead

- `AscendingTimestampExtractor` - No specific replacement specified

/**\n63:  * This is a recommended base class for all of the {@link SinkFunction} that intend to implement\n64:  * exactly-once semantic. After this point the\n180:      * transaction might still be aborted, but underlying implementation must ensure that commit\n181:      * calls on already pre committed transactions will always succeed.\n182:      *\n183:      * <p>Usually implementation involves flushing the data.\n184:      */\n185:     protected abstract void preCommit(TXN transaction) throws Exception;\n186: \n187:     /**\n188:      * Commit a pre-committed transaction. If it does not succeed eventually, a data loss will occur. Transactions will\n198:      * be recovered in an order in which they were created.\n199:      */\n200:     protected void recoverAndCommit(TXN transaction) {\n201:         commit(transaction);\n202:     }\n203: \n204:     /** Abort a transaction. */\n205:     protected abstract void abort(TXN transaction);\n206: \n207:     /** Abort a transaction that was rejected by a coordinator after a failure. */\n208:     protected void recoverAndAbort(TXN transaction) {\n209:         abort(transaction);\n210:     }\n211: \n212:     /**\n213:      * Callback for subclasses which is called after restoring (each) user context.\n214:      *\n215:      * @param handledTransactions transactions which were already committed or aborted and do not\n216:      *     need further handling\n217:      */\n218:     protected void finishRecoveringContext(Collection<TXN> handledTransactions) {}\n219: \n220:     /**\n221:      * This method is called at the end of data processing.\n222:      *\n223:      * <p>The method is expected to flush all remaining buffered data. That should be the common case.\n258:         //      Simply commit that transaction in that case.\n259:         //\n260:         //  (2) there are multiple pending transactions because one previous\n261:         //      checkpoint was skipped. That is a rare case, but can happen\n262:         //      for example when:\n263:         //\n264:         //        - the master cannot persist the metadata of the last\n265:         //          checkpoint (temporary outage in the storage system) but\n266:         //          could persist a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\n267:         //\n268:         //        - other tasks could not persist their status during\n269:         //          the previous checkpoint, but did not trigger a failure because they\n270:         //          could hold onto their state and could successfully persist it in\n271:         //          a successive checkpoint (the one notified here)\n272:         //\n273:         //      In both cases, the prior checkpoint never reach a committed state, but\n274:         //      this checkpoint is always expected to subsume the prior one and cover all\n275:         //      changes since the last successful one. As a consequence, we need to commit\n276:         //      all pending transactions.\n277:         //\n278:         //  (3) Multiple transactions are pending, but the checkpoint complete notification\n279:         //      relates not to the latest. That is possible, because notification messages\n280:         //      can be delayed (in an extreme case till arrive after a succeeding checkpoint\n281:         //      was triggered) and because there can be concurrent overlapping checkpoints\n282:         //      (a new one is started before the previous fully finished).\n283:         //\n284:         // ==> There should never be a case where we have no pending transaction here\n285:         //\n286: \n287:         Iterator<Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>>> pendingTransactionIterator =\n288:                 pendingCommitTransactions.entrySet().iterator();\n289:         Throwable firstError = null;\n290: \n291:         while (pendingTransactionIterator.hasNext()) {\n292:             Map.Entry<Long, TransactionHolder<TXN>> entry = pendingTransactionIterator.next();\n293:             Long pendingTransactionCheckpointId = entry.getKey();\n294:             TransactionHolder<TXN> pendingTransaction = entry.getValue();\n295:             if (pendingTransactionCheckpointId > checkpointId) {\n296:                 continue;\n297:             }\n298: \n299:             LOG.info(\n300:                     \"{} - checkpoint {} complete, committing transaction {} from checkpoint {}\",\n301:                     name(),\n302:                     checkpointId,\n303:                     pendingTransaction,\n304:                     pendingTransactionCheckpointId);\n305: \n306:             logWarningIfTimeoutAlmostReached(pendingTransaction);\n307:             try {\n308:                 commit(pendingTransaction.handle);\n309:             } catch (Throwable t) {\n310:                 if (firstError == null) {\n311:                     firstError = t;\n312:                 }\n313:             }\n314: \n315:             LOG.debug(\"{} - committed checkpoint transaction {}\", name(), pendingTransaction);\n316: \n317:             pendingTransactionIterator.remove();\n318:         }\n319: \n320:         if (firstError != null) {\n321:             throw new FlinkRuntimeException(\n322:                     \"Committing one of transactions failed, logging first encountered failure\",\n323:                     firstError);\n324:         }\n325:     }\n326: \n327:     @Override\n328:     public void notifyCheckpointAborted(long checkpointId) {}\n329: \n330:     @Override\n331:     public void snapshotState(FunctionSnapshotContext context) throws Exception {\n332:         // this is like the pre-commit of a 2-phase-commit transaction\n333:         // we are ready to commit and remember the transaction\n334: \n335:         long checkpointId = context.getCheckpointId();\n336:         LOG.debug(\n337:                 \"{} - checkpoint {} triggered, flushing transaction '{}'\",\n338:                 name(),\n339:                 context.getCheckpointId(),\n340:                 currentTransactionHolder);\n341: \n342:         if (currentTransactionHolder != null) {\n343:             preCommit(currentTransactionHolder.handle);\n344:             pendingCommitTransactions.put(checkpointId, currentTransactionHolder);\n345:             LOG.debug(\"{} - stored pending transactions {}\", name(), pendingCommitTransactions);\n346:         }\n347: \n348:         // no need to start new transactions after sink function is closed (no more input data)\n349:         if (!finished) {\n350:             currentTransactionHolder = beginTransactionInternal();\n351:         } else {\n352:             currentTransactionHolder = null;\n353:         }\n354:         LOG.debug(\"{} - started new transaction '{}'\", name(), currentTransactionHolder);\n355: \n356:         state.update(\n357:                 Collections.singletonList(\n358:                         new State<>(\n359:                                 this.currentTransactionHolder,\n360:                                 new ArrayList<>(pendingCommitTransactions.values()),\n361:                                 userContext)));\n362:     }\n363: \n364:     @Override\n365:     public void initializeState(FunctionInitializationContext context) throws Exception {\n366:         // when we are restoring state with pendingCommitTransactions, we don't really know whether\n367:         // the\n368:         // transactions were already committed, or whether there was a failure between\n369:         // completing the checkpoint on the master, and notifying the writer here.\n370: \n371:         // (the common case is actually that is was already committed, the window\n372:         // between the commit on the master and the notification here is very small)\n373: \n374:         // it is possible to not have any transactions at all if there was a failure before\n375:         // the first completed checkpoint, or in case of a scale-out event, where some of the\n376:         // new task do not have and transactions assigned to check)\n377: \n378:         // we can have more than one transaction to check in case of a scale-in event, or\n379:         // for the reasons discussed in the 'notifyCheckpointComplete()' method.\n380: \n381:         state = context.getOperatorStateStore().getListState(stateDescriptor);\n382: \n383:         boolean recoveredUserContext = false;\n384:         if (context.isRestored()) {\n385:             LOG.info(\"{} - restoring state\", name());\n386:             for (State<TXN, CONTEXT> operatorState : state.get()) {\n387:                 userContext = operatorState.getContext();\n388:                 List<TransactionHolder<TXN>> recoveredTransactions =\n389:                         operatorState.getPendingCommitTransactions();\n390:                 List<TXN> handledTransactions = new ArrayList<>(recoveredTransactions.size() + 1);\n391:                 for (TransactionHolder<TXN> recoveredTransaction : recoveredTransactions) {\n392:                     // If this fails to succeed eventually, there is actually data loss\n393:                     recoverAndCommitInternal(recoveredTransaction);\n394:                     handledTransactions.add(recoveredTransaction.handle);\n395:                     LOG.info(\"{} committed recovered transaction {}\", name(), recoveredTransaction);\n396:                 }\n397: \n398:                 {\n399:                     if (operatorState.getPendingTransaction() != null) {\n400:                         TXN transaction = operatorState.getPendingTransaction().handle;\n401:                         recoverAndAbort(transaction);\n402:                         handledTransactions.add(transaction);\n403:                         LOG.info(\n404:                                 \"{} aborted recovered transaction {}\",\n405:                                 name(),\n406:                                 operatorState.getPendingTransaction());\n407:                     }\n408:                 }\n409: \n410:                 if (userContext.isPresent()) {\n411:                     finishRecoveringContext(handledTransactions);\n412:                     recoveredUserContext = true;\n413:                 }\n414:             }\n415:         }\n416: \n417:         // if in restore we didn't get any userContext or we are initializing from scratch\n418:         if (!recoveredUserContext) {\n419:             LOG.info(\"{} - no state to restore\", name());\n420: \n421:             userContext = initializeUserContext();\n422:         }\n423:         this.pendingCommitTransactions.clear();\n424: \n425:         currentTransactionHolder = beginTransactionInternal();\n426:         LOG.debug(\"{} - started new transaction '{}'\", name(), currentTransactionHolder);\n427:     }\n428: \n429:     /**\n430:      * This method must be the only place to call {@link #beginTransaction()} to ensure that the\n431:      * {@link TransactionHolder} is created at the same time.\n432:      */\n433:     private TransactionHolder<TXN> beginTransactionInternal() throws Exception {\n434:         return new TransactionHolder<>(beginTransaction(), clock.millis());\n435:     }\n436: \n437:     /**\n438:      * This method must be the only place to call {@link #recoverAndCommit(Object)} to ensure that\n439:      * the configuration parameters {@link #transactionTimeout} and {@link\n440:      * #ignoreFailuresAfterTransactionTimeout} are respected.\n441:      */\n442:     private void recoverAndCommitInternal(TransactionHolder<TXN> transactionHolder) {\n443:         try {\n444:             logWarningIfTimeoutAlmostReached(transactionHolder);\n445:             recoverAndCommit(transactionHolder.handle);\n446:         } catch (final Exception e) {\n447:             final long elapsedTime = clock.millis() - transactionHolder.transactionStartTime;\n448:             if (ignoreFailuresAfterTransactionTimeout && elapsedTime > transactionTimeout) {\n449:                 LOG.error(\n450:                         \"Error while committing transaction {}. \"\n451:                                 + \"Transaction has been open for longer than the transaction timeout ({}).\"\n452:                                 + \"Commit will not be attempted again. Data loss might have occurred.\",\n453:                         transactionHolder.handle,\n454:                         transactionTimeout,\n455:                         e);\n456:             } else {\n457:                 throw e;\n458:             }\n459:         }\n460:     }\n461: \n462:     private void logWarningIfTimeoutAlmostReached(TransactionHolder<TXN> transactionHolder) {\n463:         final long elapsedTime = transactionHolder.elapsedTime(clock);\n464:         if (transactionTimeoutWarningRatio >= 0\n465:                 && elapsedTime > transactionTimeout * transactionTimeoutWarningRatio) {\n466:             LOG.warn(\n467:                     \"Transaction {} has been open for {} ms. \"\n468:                             + \"This is close to or even exceeding the transaction timeout of {} ms.\",\n469:                     transactionHolder.handle,\n470:                     elapsedTime,\n471:                     transactionTimeout);\n472:         }\n473:     }\n474: \n475:     @Override\n476:     public void close() throws Exception {\n477:         super.close();\n478: \n479:         TXN currentTransaction = currentTransaction();\n480:         if (currentTransaction != null) {\n481:             abort(currentTransaction);\n482:         }\n483: \n484:         currentTransactionHolder = null;\n485:     }\n486: \n487:     /**\n488:      * Sets the transaction timeout. By\n505:      * default, failures are propagated.\n506:      */\n507:     protected TwoPhaseCommitSinkFunction<IN, TXN, CONTEXT> ignoreFailuresAfterTransactionTimeout() {\n508:         this.ignoreFailuresAfterTransactionTimeout = true;\n509:         return this;\n510:     }\n511: \n512:     /**\n513:      * Enables logging of warnings if a transaction's elapsed time reaches a specified ratio of the\n514:      * <code>transactionTimeout</code>. org.apache.flink.streaming.api.functions.sink.legacy.SinkFunction;\\n47: import org.apache.flink.streaming.api.operators.StreamingRuntimeContext;\\n48: import org.apache.flink.util.Preconditions;\\n49: \\n50: import java.io.IOException;\\n51: import java.io.Serializable;\\n52: \\n53: /**\\n54:  * Sink that emits its input elements to {@link FileSystem} files within buckets. This is integrated\\n55:  * with the checkpointing mechanism to provide exactly once semantics.\\n56:  *\\n57:  * <p>When creating the sink a {@code basePath} must be specified. The base directory contains one\\n58:  * directory for every bucket. The bucket directories themselves contain several part files, with at\\n59:  * least one for each parallel subtask of the sink which is writing data to that bucket. These part\\n60:  * files contain the actual output data.\\n61:  *\\n62:  * <p>The sink uses a {@link BucketAssigner} to determine in which bucket directory each element\\n63:  * should be written to inside the base directory. The {@code BucketAssigner} can, for example, use\\n64:  * time or a property of the element to determine the bucket directory. The default {@code\\n65:  * BucketAssigner} is a {@link DateTimeBucketAssigner} which will create one new bucket every hour.\\n66:  * You can specify a custom {@code BucketAssigner} using the {@code\\n67:  * setBucketAssigner(bucketAssigner)} method, after calling {@link\\n68:  * StreamingFileSink#forRowFormat(Path, Encoder)} or {@link StreamingFileSink#forBulkFormat(Path,\\n69:  * BulkWriter.Factory)}.\\n70:  *\\n71:  * <p>The names of the part files could be defined using {@link OutputFileConfig}. This\\n72:  * configuration contains a part prefix and a part suffix that will be used with the parallel\\n73:  * subtask index of the sink and a rolling counter to determine the file names. For example with a\\n74:  * prefix \\\"prefix\\\" and a suffix \\\".ext\\\", a file named {@code \\\"prefix-1-17.ext\\\"} contains the data\\n75:  * from {@code subtask 1} of the sink and is the {@code 17th} bucket created by that subtask.\\n76:  *\\n77:  * <p>Part files roll based on the user-specified {@link RollingPolicy}. By default, a {@link\\n78:  * DefaultRollingPolicy} is used for row-encoded sink output; a {@link OnCheckpointRollingPolicy} is\\n79:  * used for bulk-encoded sink output.\\n80:  *\\n81:  * <p>In some scenarios, the open buckets are required to change based on time. In these cases, the\\n82:  * user can specify a {@code bucketCheckInterval} (by default 1m) and the sink will check\\n83:  * periodically and roll the part file if the specified rolling policy says so.\\n84:  *\\n85:  * <p>Part files can be in one of three states: {@code in-progress}, {@code pending} or {@code\\n86:  * finished}. The reason for this is how the sink works together with the checkpointing mechanism to\\n87:  * provide exactly-once semantics and fault-tolerance. The part file that is currently being written\\n88:  * to is {@code in-progress}. Once a part file is closed for writing it becomes {@code pending}.\\n89:  * When a checkpoint is successful the currently pending files will be moved to {@code finished}.\\n90:  *\\n91:  * <p>If case of a failure, and in order to guarantee exactly-once semantics, the sink should roll\\n92:  * back to the state it had when that last successful checkpoint occurred. To this end, when\\n93:  * restoring, the restored files in {@code pending} state are transferred into the {@code finished}\\n94:  * state while any {@code in-progress} files are rolled back, so that they do not contain data that\\n95:  * arrived after the checkpoint from which we restore.\\n96:  *\\n97:  * @param <IN> Type of the elements emitted by this sink\\n98:  * @deprecated Use {@link org.apache.flink.connector.file.sink.FileSink} instead.\\n99:  */\\n100: @Internal\\n101: public class StreamingFileSink<IN> extends RichSinkFunction<IN>\\n102:         implements CheckpointedFunction, CheckpointListener {\\n103: \\n104:     private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L;\\n105: \\n106:     // ------------------------ configuration fields --------------------------\\n107: \\n108:     private final long bucketCheckInterval;\\n109: \\n110:     private final BucketsBuilder<IN, ?, ? \n50: import java.io.IOException;\n51: import java.io.Serializable;\n52: \n53: /**\n54:  * Sink that emits its input elements to {@link FileSystem} files within buckets. This is integrated\n55:  * with the checkpointing mechanism to provide exactly once semantics.\n56:  *\n57:  * <p>When creating the sink a {@code basePath} must be specified. The base directory contains one\n58:  * directory for every bucket. The bucket directories themselves contain several part files, with at\n59:  * least one for each parallel subtask of the sink which is writing data to that bucket. These part\n60:  * files contain the actual output data.\n61:  *\n62:  * <p>The sink uses a {@link BucketAssigner} to determine in which bucket directory each element\n63:  * should be written to inside the base directory. The {@code BucketAssigner} can, for example, use\n64:  * time or a property of the element to determine the bucket directory. The default {@code\n65:  * BucketAssigner} is a {@link DateTimeBucketAssigner} which will create one new bucket every hour.\n66:  * You can specify a custom {@code BucketAssigner} using the {@code\n67:  * setBucketAssigner(bucketAssigner)} method, after calling {@link\n68:  * StreamingFileSink#forRowFormat(Path, Encoder)} or {@link StreamingFileSink#forBulkFormat(Path,\n69:  * BulkWriter.Factory)}.\n70:  *\n71:  * <p>The names of the part files could be defined using {@link OutputFileConfig}. This\n72:  * configuration contains a part prefix and a part suffix that will be used with the parallel\n73:  * subtask index of the sink and a rolling counter to determine the file names. For example with a\n74:  * prefix \"prefix\" and a suffix \".ext\", a file named {@code \"prefix-1-17.ext\"} contains the data\n75:  * from {@code subtask 1} of the sink and is the {@code 17th} bucket created by that subtask.\n76:  *\n77:  * <p>Part files roll based on the user-specified {@link RollingPolicy}. By default, a {@link\n78:  * DefaultRollingPolicy} is used for row-encoded sink output; a {@link OnCheckpointRollingPolicy} is\n79:  * used for bulk-encoded sink output.\n80:  *\n81:  * <p>In some scenarios, the open buckets are required to change based on time. In these cases, the\n82:  * user can specify a {@code bucketCheckInterval} (by default 1m) and the sink will check\n83:  * periodically and roll the part file if the specified rolling policy says so.\n84:  *\n85:  * <p>Part files can be in one of three states: {@code in-progress}, {@code pending} or {@code\n86:  * finished}. The reason for this is how the sink works together with the checkpointing mechanism to\n87:  * provide exactly-once semantics and fault-tolerance. The part file that is currently being written\n88:  * to is {@code in-progress}. Once a part file is closed for writing it becomes {@code pending}.\n89:  * When a checkpoint is successful the currently pending files will be moved to {@code finished}.\n90:  *\n91:  * <p>If case of a failure, and in order to guarantee exactly-once semantics, the sink should roll\n92:  * back to the state it had when that last successful checkpoint occurred. To this end, when\n93:  * restoring, the restored files in {@code pending} state are transferred into the {@code finished}\n94:  * state while any {@code in-progress} files are rolled back, so that they do not contain data that\n95:  * arrived after the checkpoint from which we restore.\n96:  *\n97:  * @param <IN> Type of the elements emitted by this sink\n98:  * @deprecated Use {@link org.apache.flink.connector.file.sink.FileSink} instead.\n99:  */\n100: @Internal\n101: public class StreamingFileSink<IN> extends RichSinkFunction<IN>\n102:         implements CheckpointedFunction, CheckpointListener {\n103: \n104:     private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L;\n105: \n106:     // ------------------------ configuration fields --------------------------\n107: \n108:     private final long bucketCheckInterval;\n109: \n110:     private final BucketsBuilder<IN, ?, ?
